## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction, where dA_dt represents the rate of change of concentration A. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as a function of concentration A (and sometimes explicitly of time for non-elementary or externally driven processes).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (transition between zero and first order)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate with equilibrium)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (externally driven linear kinetics)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative rate law)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular reaction rate)
- Half-integer order: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (chain reaction mechanism, half-order)
- Combined rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate depends only on A (not t) → autonomous ODE, suggesting elementary or pseudo-elementary rate law: dA_dt = f(A)
- Rate proportional to integer power of A → elementary reaction with molecularity equal to the power
- Rate with fractional power of A → chain reaction mechanism or surface-mediated process
- Rate with polynomial in A (multiple terms) → parallel reaction pathways or reversible reactions with conservation laws
- Rate with rational function of A → enzyme-like or saturation kinetics where a limiting step controls the rate
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system such as photolysis, temperature ramp, or catalyst deactivation
- Sign of rate law terms → negative terms indicate consumption, positive terms indicate production or reverse reaction
- Rate = f(A) with f having a root at positive A → existence of equilibrium concentration where reaction stops
- Quadratic dependence A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or bimolecular reaction where second species is related to A via conservation law
